< review>
Loved that I could book and pay online. That is all the praise I can give because the couples massage + body scrub treatment was a disappointing waste of $120 (+ tip) and 60 minutes. What I expected - partially due to past experiences at other spas and partially due to their vague description of services - was a 1 hour full body massage and body scrub. What I got was 45 minutes of rubbing lotion into my back, punctuated by a painfully hot stone massage, and about 15 minutes of light massage for my head, arms, and legs. Though I encouraged my massage therapist to use more pressure there was a definite language barrier there, and it just didn't happen. On top of that whatever music they had playing in the background kept getting interrupted by a male voice loudly speaking in Chinese, which was less than relaxing. One of the ladies working on us kept trying to fix it to no avail. And the scrub? Confined to my back and shoulders only, and lasted all of about 2 minutes.

It's just disappointing. I've still got the same aches and pains that I started out the day with, and instead of being relaxed I'm annoyed. This was supposed to be a nice treat for my boyfriend and myself after a really demanding month, and it just wasn't. The receptionist was sure to tell us a positive review about net us a $20 credit, but so what when the best I can say is that I'm not in more pain now than I was before I walked in and I could book and pay online? There's no way we're going back and wasting even more time and money at this place, and I certainly will not recommend it to anyone.</review>

< Text>
This restaurant discriminates against disabled people!!!

If you have a certified service dog for any disability other than blindness they literally will NOT SERVE you.

This is ILLEGAL, not to mention extremely rude and unethical.

The Americans with Disabilities Act is very clear about federal requirements:

‚ÄúUnder the ADA, State and local governments, businesses, and nonprofit organizations that serve the public generally must allow service animals to accompany people with disabilities in all areas of the facility where the public is normally allowed to go. ‚Äù (ada.gov)

Relevantly, it also states precisely that

‚ÄúEstablishments that sell or prepare food must allow service animals in public areas even if state or local health codes prohibit animals on the premises.‚Äù (ada.gov)

The fact that the owner of this business refused to serve me because of my service dog is a blatant act of discrimination and a display of abhorring customer service.

Ignorance of the law or inability to understand it are not an acceptable justification for this type of behavior.<//Text>

If you order a medium size Chicken Teriyaki Bowl Combo you should get 2 Egg Rolls & a medium size drink.  If you order a large size, you should get 3 Egg Rolls & a large size drink.

Fair is fair.< /text>
